Summary of Key Trends in Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX)

This analysis was conducted to identify key trends in the AI transformation (AX) of the manufacturing industry.
The most significant trend is 'intelligent autonomy,' moving beyond simple automation. This is driven by 'Agentic AI' and 'Physical AI' technologies that analyze data, make judgments, and execute actions independently. Enhanced autonomy of industrial robots and the concept of Software-Defined Factory (SDF) support this.

The second key trend is the proliferation of 'Digital Twin' technology. The practice of replicating physical factories in virtual spaces to simulate various scenarios and make optimal decisions based on these simulations is becoming widespread. Beyond traditional areas such as semiconductor defect detection, predictive maintenance, and vision inspection, AI's application is expanding across the entire value chain, including new material discovery and supply chain financial analysis.

While these changes offer opportunities for maximizing productivity and securing supply chain stability, they also present challenges such as cyber security threats stemming from the adoption of generative AI and the need for in-house development of core robot hardware technology.

Ultimately, manufacturing AX aims for an 'intelligent autonomous factory' that operates independently based on data, and successful transformation requires the integration of AI technologies, along with the establishment of security governance and the securing of core technological competitiveness.

Accenture's Physical AI Orchestrator is a means of realizing a 'software-defined factory' by combining Nvidia Omniverse-based digital twin and physical simulation with AI agents to pre-verify layouts, resource allocation, and safety rules, and connect the results to work instructions, robot paths, and equipment parameters. Based on proven effects (warehouse throughput +20%, CapEx -15%), it can be immediately applied to warehouse layout/picking path optimization, line balancing, virtual safety fences, and refrigeration/storage cycle optimization, while reality capture, vision, IoT/OT integration, and a human-in-the-loop approval system are essential prerequisites.

Accenture's Physical AI Orchestrator is a 'software-defined factory' platform that combines digital twin, Omniverse simulation, and agentic AI to virtually verify changes to factory and warehouse operations and connect the results to on-site directives. In actual cases, quantitative results such as a 20% improvement in throughput and a 15% reduction in CapEx were confirmed, and its application scope is wide, including robot safety fences and preservation cycle optimization. When adopting it, reality capture, vision-based data collection, IT/OT integration, and human-in-the-loop governance are key, and suitable initial application tasks include layout/line balancing/safety zone/storage cycle optimization. KPIs recommend throughput, lead time, OEE, safety, and energy/CapEx reduction.

This review presents a practical framework that maps deep learning, reinforcement learning, and generative models across the entire wafer front-end process to implement defect detection, quality prediction, process regime classification, and autonomous control, complementing existing FDC/SPC/APC to increase anomaly detection sensitivity and reduce false positives. Additionally, it organizes methods for mitigating tool dynamics and environmental disturbances in crystal growth, slicing, and ultra-precision machining with AI-based predictive control, to a level applicable across precision manufacturing. The implementation roadmap is presented as starting from processes with high CTQ/defect contribution, leading through vision/sensor PoC â†’ alleviation of data constraints via synthetic data and transfer learning â†’ to the expansion of RL/MPC-based R2R closed-loop optimization on edge-cloud+MLOps. Concurrently, implement inline metrology, high-frequency sensor fusion, and standard tagging, and quantify the effects using yield, CT, utilization, scrap, energy, and COQ KPIs.

This article is a systematically organized review of methods for applying AI to the entire wafer manufacturing process and their expected effects, explaining deep learning, reinforcement learning, and generative models connected respectively to defect detection, autonomous process control, and mitigation of data scarcity. Implementation-centric points such as integration with FDC/SPC/APC, real-time edge inference, data acquisition and labeling strategies, and digital twins are clear, and a phased roadmap leading from PoC to closed-loop control to entire process optimization is useful in practice. Strategies such as sensor fusion, synthetic data, and transfer learning predicated on data constraints and environmental disturbances, along with KPI (yield, CT, uptime)-centric goal setting, provide practical execution guidelines.

Industrial robots are transitioning from 'automation' to 'autonomy' through the integration of AI, computer vision, and digital twin. Pilot projects by BMW, Mercedes, and Tesla are demonstrating the implementation of flexibility in high-mix, low-volume production. Manufacturing sites should build an end-to-end architecture connecting robot controllers, vision/sensors, path planning, edge AI, and fleet orchestration with MES/PLM/SCADA, and verify ROI at each stage using digital twin-based offline programming and KPIs (CT, OEE, FPY, HSE). Traditional articulated robots are effective for cycle-time-centric processes, while cobots and humanoids are best applied preferentially for unstructured, frequently changing tasks and during night or staffing-gap shifts.

ë³´ê³ ì„œëŠ” ì‚°ì—…ìš© ë¡œë´‡ì´ AIÂ·ë¹„ì „Â·ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆê³¼ ê²°í•©í•´ â€˜ìë™í™”â†’ììœ¨í™”â€™ë¡œ ì§„í™”í•˜ëŠ” íë¦„ì„ ì •ë¦¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ìë™ì°¨Â·ì „ì ì„ ë„ ì‚¬ë¡€ì™€ ì½”ë´‡/íœ´ë¨¸ë…¸ì´ë“œ íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿, ëª¨ë“ˆëŸ¬ ì•” í™•ì‚°, íˆ¬ì í™•ëŒ€ê°€ í•µì‹¬ ë™í–¥ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ì—ì„  1) ê³ ìœ„í—˜Â·ê³ ë³€ë™ ê³µì •ë¶€í„° íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿, 2) ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆ ê¸°ë°˜ ì‹œë®¬ë ˆì´ì…˜/ì˜¤í”„ë¼ì¸ í”„ë¡œê·¸ë˜ë°, 3) MES/PLM ì—°ë™ ë° ì—£ì§€ AI ë¹„ì „ ìŠ¤íƒ í†µí•©, 4) ISO 10218/TS 15066 ì•ˆì „ ì¤€ìˆ˜ì™€ IEC 62443 ë³´ì•ˆì„ ë³‘í–‰í•˜ëŠ” ì „ëµì´ ìœ íš¨í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. KPI(OEEÂ·FPYÂ·CTÂ·HSE)ë¡œ ë‹¨ê³„ë³„ ROIë¥¼ ê²€ì¦í•˜ê³ , í‘œì¤€ ì¸í„°í˜ì´ìŠ¤(OPC UA/ROSâ€‘I)ì™€ ëª¨ë“ˆëŸ¬ ì—”ë“œì´í™í„°ë¡œ ì¬í™œìš©ì„±ì„ ë†’ì´ë©´ TCOë¥¼ ë‚®ì¶œ ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ì½”ë´‡/íœ´ë¨¸ë…¸ì´ë“œì˜ ì´ˆê¸° ê°€ì¹˜ëŠ” ë¹„ì •í˜• ë³´ì¡° ì‘ì—…ê³¼ ì¸ë ¥ ê³µë°± ëŒ€ì‘ì— ìˆìœ¼ë©°, ë°ì´í„° ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤Â·MLOps ì²´ê³„ê°€ ìê¸°í•™ìŠµ ë¡œë´‡ì˜ ì„±ê³¼ë¥¼ ì¢Œìš°í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. The report summarizes the trend of industrial robots evolving from 'automation' to 'autonomy' through their combination with AI, vision, and digital twin technologies. Key trends include leading cases in automotive and electronics, cobot/humanoid pilots, the proliferation of modular arms, and increased investment. In manufacturing sites, an effective strategy involves: 1) piloting high-risk, high-variability processes, 2) digital twin-based simulation/offline programming, 3) MES/PLM integration and edge AI vision stack integration, and 4) combining ISO 10218/TS 15066 safety compliance with IEC 62443 security. By verifying phased ROI with KPIs (OEE, FPY, CT, HSE) and increasing reusability with standard interfaces (OPC UA/ROS-I) and modular end-effectors, Total Cost of Ownership (TCO) can be lowered. The initial value of cobots/humanoids lies in unstructured auxiliary tasks and addressing labor shortages, while data governance and MLOps systems determine the performance of self-learning robots.

Hyundai Motor India's CMO message presents a smart factory implementation roadmap that aims for zero defects by connecting 2,000 facilities with IIoT, managing 20 billion data points and 300+ process parameters in real-time annually, and utilizing deep learning vision, AI specification verification, and end-to-end process traceability. Key implementation points include standard data models and an integrated data lake/mesh, anomaly detection KPI-based dashboards, Vision AI PoC to standardization and MLOps, and closed-loop synchronization of product and process digital twins. Furthermore, it provides quantitative indicators of manufacturing competitiveness, encompassing flexible production of 14 models/450+ trims, supply chain resilience through 81.7% localization and battery assembly, and ESG internalization, such as 88% renewable energy and a 41.8% reduction in Scope 1/2 emissions.

Hyundai Motor India, under the SDF vision, connected 2,000 pieces of equipment with IIoT (20 billion data points annually), managed 300+ process parameters in real-time, and digitized quality through deep learning vision, AI specification verification, and end-to-end process traceability. Practical points to be applied in the manufacturing field are data platform standardization and real-time visualization, an MLOps system for AI vision, digital twin-based closed-loop quality/production optimization, platform design for multi-model flexible production, and the establishment of localization and supplier co-development governance.

The core value of the article is that it presents a direction for implementing trustworthy agentic AI in manufacturing sites using 'understanding-based AI' and the O-A-P (Observe-Analyze-Prescribe) framework. Data should be handled not more, but smarter (context, modeling, governance), and AI should be designed as a partner that amplifies expert judgment. Practically, important elements include the establishment of standardized industrial data models, the preparation of real-time observation layers and root cause analysis playbooks, approval and tracking systems for prescribed actions, and verification processes that link ROI to 'AI intervention and KPI changes'. Through this, closed-loop optimization of key indicators such as quality, yield, and energy can be pursued.

China's 90% localization of robot hardware and in-house production of core components (reducers, servos, controllers, high-precision sensors), combined with its advantages in AI/data and talent, is simultaneously improving cost, lead time, and quality, thereby rapidly accelerating physical AI-based manufacturing automation (process, logistics, assembly). The paper proposes a framework for managing supply chain resilience by connecting production metrics (equipment utilization rate, productivity ratio, output variability) with financial metrics (liquidity, working capital, cash conversion cycle) through machine learning predictions and financial stress tests. This enables quantifying cash requirements, service levels, and recovery time during demand and supply shocks, and optimizing SCF policies such as dynamic discounting, reverse factoring, and inventory financing on a risk-based approach. It is useful for integrating financial resilience KPIs into monthly decision-making by embedding them into S&OP/IBP, and for comparing and deciding the ROI of investment alternatives (diversification, safety stock, lead time reduction) by scenario. A phased implementation in the sequence of data pipeline alignment, ML predictions, stress models, policy automation, and model risk management is recommended.

The digital thread connecting aerospace new materials (CMC, TiAl, Mg-Li, recycled carbon fiber) and AM with AI integrates design-manufacturing-verification, reducing development lead time from years to months, saving testing and inspection costs by approximately 35%, and driving fuel and COâ‚‚ savings through 15-20% improved CMC-based thermal efficiency and up to 50% lightweighting (Mg-Li ~35%). Closed-loop control, combining AM's part consolidation, internal channels, multi-material capabilities with in-line monitoring (melt pool/thermal imaging) and ML quality prediction, is key to ROI. Recycled carbon fiber (95% strength recovery) and bio-composites (~40% reduction in environmental impact) are effective for the circular economy and Scope 3 reduction. Execution should proceed in the following sequence: establishing a material-process data lake/standard schema â†’ collecting composite and AM sensor data/PoC for defect detection â†’ scaling up and ensuring regulatory compliance through SPC/CPK, process simulation, and model-based certification.

Advanced materials for aerospace (CMC, TiAl, Mg-Li, recycled carbon fiber) and the proliferation of AM are driving fuel efficiency, lightweighting, and carbon reduction, and the core of AX underpinning this is the integration of data-driven design-manufacturing-verification and AI/automation. As the rapid adoption of GenAI in manufacturing converges with attacks exploiting trusted cloud services (OneDrive, GitHub), security operations focused on visibility and control are essential for protecting critical assets such as CAD, BOM, process recipes, PLC configurations, and source code/API keys. With an enterprise GenAI gateway/proxy, unify prompt and response logging, DLP, and secret information masking, and in conjunction with CASB/SSPM, apply download inspection, external sharing blocking, and personal cloud/unauthorized AI app blocking. For agentic AI, implement task scope limitations, guardrails, and approval workflows, and reflect prompt injection and data exfiltration countermeasures in the IR playbook.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì œì¡° ê¸°ì—…ì˜ GenAI í™œìš©ì´ ê¸‰ì¦í•˜ë©´ì„œ ê³µê²© í‘œë©´ì´ í™•ëŒ€ë˜ê³ , OneDriveÂ·GitHub ë“± ì‹ ë¢° í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ ì•…ìš©ê³¼ ê°œì¸ í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ ì‚¬ìš©ì´ ë°ì´í„° ìœ ì¶œì˜ ì£¼ëœ í†µë¡œê°€ ë˜ê³  ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. íŠ¹íˆ ê·œì œ ë°ì´í„°, ì†ŒìŠ¤ì½”ë“œ, ë¹„ë°€ë²ˆí˜¸/API í‚¤ ë…¸ì¶œ ìœ„í—˜ì´ í½ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤ë¬´ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ìŠ¹ì¸ëœ GenAI ì•± ì¤‘ì‹¬ìœ¼ë¡œ ì „í™˜í•˜ê³ , í”„ë¡ì‹œ/ê²Œì´íŠ¸ì›¨ì´ë¥¼ í†µí•œ í”„ë¡¬í”„íŠ¸Â·ì‘ë‹µ ë¡œê¹…ê³¼ DLP ì ìš©, ìœ„í—˜ ì•± ì°¨ë‹¨, ë‹¤ìš´ë¡œë“œ ê²€ì‚¬ ê°•í™”ê°€ ì¤‘ìš”í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì—ì´ì „í‹± AIëŠ” ì‘ì—… ë²”ìœ„Â·ê°€ë“œë ˆì¼Â·ìŠ¹ì¸ ì ˆì°¨ë¡œ ì œì–´í•˜ê³ , ë ˆí¬ì§€í† ë¦¬ ë¹„ë°€ ìŠ¤ìºë‹ê³¼ ì»¤ë°‹ í›…ìœ¼ë¡œ í‚¤ ìœ ì¶œì„ ì°¨ë‹¨í•˜ì„¸ìš”. ë„ë©´/BOM/ê³µì •ë ˆì‹œí”¼ ë“± ì œì¡° í•µì‹¬ ìì‚°ì„ DLP ë¶„ë¥˜ì— í¬í•¨í•˜ê³ , IT-OT ì œë¡œíŠ¸ëŸ¬ìŠ¤íŠ¸ ë° IR í”Œë ˆì´ë¶(í”„ë¡¬í”„íŠ¸ ì£¼ì…/ëª¨ë¸ ì˜¤ë‚¨ìš© ëŒ€ì‘)ì„ ì—…ë°ì´íŠ¸í•˜ë©´ GenAI ì‹œëŒ€ì— ë§ëŠ” ë³´ì•ˆ íƒ„ë ¥ì„±ì„ í™•ë³´í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. As the use of GenAI by manufacturing companies rapidly increases, the attack surface expands, and the misuse of trusted cloud services like OneDrive and GitHub, along with the use of personal cloud services, are becoming the primary channels for data leakage. In particular, the risk of exposure of regulated data, source code, and passwords/API keys is significant. Practically, it is crucial to transition to approved GenAI apps, apply prompt and response logging and DLP through proxies/gateways, block risky apps, and strengthen download inspections. Agentic AI should be controlled with defined work scopes, guardrails, and approval procedures, and key leakage should be prevented through repository secret scanning and commit hooks. By including critical manufacturing assets like drawings, BOMs (Bills of Materials), and process recipes in DLP classifications, and updating IT-OT Zero Trust and IR playbooks (for prompt injection/model misuse response), you can secure security resilience suitable for the GenAI era.

To cope with mixed-model production (ICE/HEV/EV), adopt modular cells and standardized mechanical and electrical/electronic interfaces, and combine AMR/AGV + intelligent sequencing and supermarket/picking redesign to simultaneously reduce changeover and bottlenecks through flow-based material supply. AI vision boosts FPY through a hybrid approach of dataset quality management (including label accuracy, lighting/angle diversity) and continuous re-learning (MLOps), as well as edge inference + cloud model management. MES, ERP, and WMS secure real-time decision-making and connectivity through event streaming (MQTT/Kafka), an API-first approach, and standardization of master data/equipment tags. Human-centric automation combines collaborative robot risk assessment (ISO/TS 15066), ergonomics, and digital work instructions/upskilling. Based on core KPIs (OEE, changeover, FPY/scrap, intralogistics lead time/on-time, MTTR/safety), pursue a pilot-to-expansion roadmap and partnership governance.

This article defines a 'true' digital twin not as mere visualization, but as an AI operational layer equipped with real-time data contextualization and interoperability (ERP/MES/DCS/Historian/LIMS/QMS). In a GMP environment, it proposes lifecycle governance including CSV/GAMP-based model validation, ALCOA+ data integrity, change management, traceability, audit trails, and MLOps. By reconfiguring Continuous Process Verification (CPV) as a twin, it realizes predictive quality, deviation prevention, closed-loop optimization, and multi-site technology transfer, and provides a practical path to achieving real-time quality assurance and accelerated batch release. It suggests starting implementation with use cases prioritized and managing KPIs such as batch release lead time, deviation rate, CPV alert accuracy, OEE/yield, and early drift detection.

ë³¸ ë…¼ë¬¸ì€ ì—ì´ì „í‹± AIì˜ ê³„ì¸µí˜• ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜(ì§€ê°â€“ê³„íš/ì¶”ë¡ â€“íˆ´ ì‹¤í–‰/ì•¡ì¶”ì—ì´ì…˜â€“í”¼ë“œë°±/ë°˜ì„±â€“ë©”ëª¨ë¦¬/RAGâ€“ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤)ë¥¼ ì œì¡° AXì— ì ìš©í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆëŠ” ì„¤ê³„ ê¸°ì¤€ìœ¼ë¡œ ì œì‹œí•˜ë©°, IoT ê¸°ë°˜ ì˜ˆì§€ì •ë¹„Â·í’ˆì§ˆ ê²€ì‚¬Â·ìƒì‚°ê³„íš/ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ë§ì„ ë©€í‹°ì—ì´ì „íŠ¸ë¡œ ìë™ ì˜¤ì¼€ìŠ¤íŠ¸ë ˆì´ì…˜í•˜ê³  MES/ERP/SCADA/CMMSì™€ APIÂ·OPC UA ì—°ë™ì„ í†µí•´ ì‹¤ì œ ì‘ì—…ì§€ì‹œÂ·íŒŒë¼ë¯¸í„° ì¡°ì •ê¹Œì§€ ìˆ˜í–‰í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ìŠ¹ì¸ ê²Œì´íŠ¸Â·ê¶Œí•œ ìŠ¤ì½”í”„Â·ì„¤ëª…ê°€ëŠ¥ ë¡œê·¸ ë“± ì•ˆì „ ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ë¥¼ ì „ì œë¡œ ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì • ì§€ì—°ì„ ì‹œê°„ ë‹¨ìœ„ì—ì„œ ì´ˆ ë‹¨ìœ„ë¡œ ë‹¨ì¶•í•˜ê³  ë¹„ê³„íš ë‹¤ìš´íƒ€ì„ì„ ìµœëŒ€ 30% ì¤„ì´ëŠ” ë“± KPI ê°œì„ ì´ ê°€ëŠ¥í•˜ë©°, ì—£ì§€+ì¤‘ì•™ í˜¼í•© ë°°ì¹˜ì™€ ë‹¨ê³„ì  ë„ì… ë¡œë“œë§µì„ ì œê³µí•´ ì‹¤ë¬´ ì ìš©ì„±ì„ ë†’ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. This paper proposes a hierarchical architecture of agentic AI (perception â€“ planning/reasoning â€“ tool execution/actuation â€“ feedback/reflection â€“ memory/RAG â€“ governance) as a design standard applicable to manufacturing AX, and automatically orchestrates IoT-based predictive maintenance, quality inspection, and production planning/scheduling with multi-agents. It also performs actual work orders and parameter adjustments through API and OPC UA integration with MES/ERP/SCADA/CMMS. Predicated on safety governance such as approval gates, authorization scopes, and explainable logs, it enables KPI improvements such as shortening decision-making delays from hours to seconds and reducing unplanned downtime by up to 30%. Furthermore, it enhances practical applicability by offering a hybrid deployment of edge and central systems and a phased adoption roadmap.

The paper systematizes the core architecture, governance, and evaluation metrics of agentic AI, making it useful as manufacturing AX design guidelines. The key to manufacturing application is closed-loop automation, which integrates IoT/vision data into the perception layer and enables agents to safely execute actions such as work orders, equipment parameter changes, and inventory movements by interfacing with MES/CMMS/SCADA. In particular, it provides practical implications to shorten decision-making delays by applying multi-agents to predictive maintenance, quality optimization, and production scheduling (Practical KPIs: automatic processing rate, MTBF/MTTR, throughput, energy unit cost), and to ensure safety with policies, approval gates, and explainable logs. Implementation directions such as edge deployment and RAG-based knowledge integration are also presented, offering high immediate reference value for manufacturing sites.

ë„¤ì˜¤ì œì¡° ì¸í…”ë¦¬ì „ìŠ¤(NFI)ëŠ” ì¤‘ì•™ ê·œì¹™ê¸°ë°˜ ìë™í™”ë¥¼ ë¶„ì‚°Â·í™•ë¥ ì Â·ìê°€í•™ìŠµ ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜(RLÂ·ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆÂ·ì—°í•©/ì˜¨ë¼ì¸ í•™ìŠµ+ì—£ì§€-í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ)ë¡œ ì „í™˜í•´ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì •ê³¼ ììœ¨ ì¬êµ¬ì„±ì„ ê°€ëŠ¥ì¼€ í•˜ë©°, ìˆ˜ìš” ë³€ë™Â·ìì¬ ì´ì§ˆì„±Â·ê³µê¸‰ë§ ì¶©ê²© í•˜ì—ì„œë„ ìœ ì—°ì„± í–¥ìƒÂ·ë‹¤ìš´íƒ€ì„ ê°ì†ŒÂ·ì²˜ë¦¬ëŸ‰ ê°œì„ ì„ ì œê³µí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤ë¬´ ì ìš© ì‹œ ì¬êµ¬ì„± ì§€ì—°, ë™ì  ì…ë ¥ ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì • ì •í™•ë„, ì˜ˆì§€ì •ë¹„ ì˜ˆì¸¡ ì •í™•ë„ ë“±ì˜ KPIë¥¼ ì¶”ì í•˜ê³ , ì„¼ì„œ/ì—£ì§€â†’ì „ì²˜ë¦¬Â·ë¶„ì‚°ì €ì¥â†’ì—°ì†í•™ìŠµ ì—ì´ì „íŠ¸â†’í”¼ë“œë°±â†’ì¬ì„¤ì •/ì¬êµ¬ì„± ëª…ë ¹(ì˜ˆ: OPC UA/MQTT) íŒ¨í„´ìœ¼ë¡œ êµ¬ì¶•í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ ìœ íš¨í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë˜í•œ ISO 23247Â·IEC 62264 ì •í•©ê³¼ SHAP/LIME ê¸°ë°˜ ì„¤ëª…ê°€ëŠ¥ì„± í™•ë³´, ë°ì´í„° í’ˆì§ˆÂ·ì„¼ì„œ ì¥ì• Â·ë³´ì•ˆ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ì— ëŒ€í•œ ë°ì´í„° ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤Â·ëª¨ë¸ ê²€ì¦ ê²Œì´íŒ…Â·Human-in-the-LoopÂ·ì œë¡œíŠ¸ëŸ¬ìŠ¤íŠ¸/ëª¨ë¸ ì„œëª… ì ìš©ì„ ë³‘í–‰í•˜ì‹­ì‹œì˜¤. Neo-Manufacturing Intelligence (NFI) transforms central rule-based automation into a distributed, probabilistic, self-learning architecture (RL, Digital Twin, Federated/Online Learning + Edge-Cloud), enabling real-time decision-making and autonomous reconfiguration, and providing enhanced flexibility, reduced downtime, and improved throughput even amidst demand fluctuations, material heterogeneity, and supply chain shocks. In practical application, it is effective to track KPIs such as reconfiguration delay, dynamic input decision accuracy, and predictive maintenance accuracy, and to build it with a pattern of Sensor/Edge â†’ Preprocessing Â· Distributed Storage â†’ Continuous Learning Agent â†’ Feedback â†’ Reset/Reconfiguration Commands (e.g., OPC UA/MQTT). Additionally, ensure alignment with ISO 23247 and IEC 62264 and secure explainability based on SHAP/LIME; for data quality, sensor failures, and security risks, simultaneously apply data governance, model validation gating, Human-in-the-Loop, and Zero-Trust/Model Signing.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ë…¼ë¬¸ì€ ìê¸°í•™ìŠµí˜• ìƒì‚° ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜(NFI)ë¥¼ í†µí•´ ê³µì¥ì´ ê·œì¹™ê¸°ë°˜ì—ì„œ í™•ë¥ ì Â·ì˜ˆì¸¡í˜• ìš´ì˜ìœ¼ë¡œ ì „í™˜ë˜ëŠ” í”„ë ˆì„ì„ ì œì‹œí•œë‹¤. ì¬êµ¬ì„± ì§€ì—°, ë™ì  ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì • ì •í™•ë„, ìˆ˜ìš” ë³€ë™ í•˜ ì²˜ë¦¬ëŸ‰, ì˜ˆì§€ì •ë¹„ ì •í™•ë„ ë“± AX ì„±ê³¼ KPIë¥¼ ëª…í™•íˆ í•˜ì˜€ê³ , RLÂ·ì—°í•©í•™ìŠµÂ·GNNÂ·ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆÂ·ì—£ì§€ ë¶„ì„ê³¼ OPC UA/MQTT ë“± êµ¬í˜„ ìŠ¤íƒì„ êµ¬ì²´í™”í–ˆë‹¤. ë˜í•œ ISO 23247Â·IEC 62264 ì •í•©ì„±, SHAP/LIME ê¸°ë°˜ ì„¤ëª…ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±, ê°ì‚¬ë¡œê·¸ ë“± í’ˆì§ˆ/ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ ì‹¤ë¬´ í¬ì¸íŠ¸ë¥¼ ì œì‹œí•´ ì ìš© ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ë†’ë‹¤. ë‹¤ë§Œ ì •ëŸ‰ ì‚¬ë¡€ëŠ” ë¶€ì¡±í•˜ë¯€ë¡œ, ì˜ˆì§€ì •ë¹„Â·ë™ì  ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ë§ íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿ì—ì„œ ì‹œì‘í•´ ë‹¤ê³µì¥ ì—°í•©í•™ìŠµìœ¼ë¡œ í™•ì¥í•˜ëŠ” ë‹¨ê³„ì  ë„ì…ì´ í˜„ì‹¤ì ì´ë‹¤. The paper presents a framework for factories to transition from rule-based to probabilistic and predictive operations through a self-learning production architecture (NFI). It clarified AX performance KPIs such as reconfiguration delay, dynamic decision-making accuracy, throughput under demand fluctuations, and predictive maintenance accuracy, and specified the implementation stack including RL, federated learning, GNN, digital twin, edge analytics, and OPC UA/MQTT. In addition, by presenting practical points for quality and governance, such as conformance with ISO 23247 and IEC 62264, SHAP/LIME-based explainability, and audit logs, its applicability is high. However, as quantitative examples are lacking, a phased introduction is realistic, starting with predictive maintenance and dynamic scheduling pilots and expanding to multi-factory federated learning.

This case demonstrates that by compressing the existing 7-12 day process into 6 hours through closed-system and semi-automated CAR-T manufacturing, lead time and cost can be significantly reduced, and quality consistency and clinical efficacy can be simultaneously secured by maintaining T-cells in a less differentiated state. From a manufacturing AX perspective, key implementation points include single-use based closed-system modules (e.g., Sepax), minimization of cleanroom requirements and logistics, multi-site expansion through standardized equipment, recipes, and data models, and implementing operational automation such as predictive release and anomaly detection by linking real-time PATâ€“MES/EBR and AI-based condition optimization.

This is a case where CAR-T was produced within 6 hours using a closed-system and semi-automated process, without 7 days of culture, showing equivalent or better performance compared to the standard process. From a manufacturing AX perspective, key elements include closed-module based design, cycle time compression, reproducibility of scale transfer, and CQA alignment from a QbD perspective. To support this, combining AI/digitalization such as real-time PAT, MES/EBR, anomaly detection, and schedule optimization can simultaneously improve cost, quality, and speed. Designing equipment standardization, stable supply of disposable consumables, and data integrity/validation strategies together is key to practical success.

AI ì„œë²„ í˜¸í™©ìœ¼ë¡œ HBMÂ·CoWoS/2.5D/3D íŒ¨í‚¤ì§•Â·í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ê³µì •ì´ ë³‘ëª©ì´ ë˜ë¯€ë¡œ ìˆ˜ìœ¨ê´€ë¦¬ ì²´ê³„ ê°•í™”ì™€ ì¥ë¹„ ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„/ìºíŒŒ í™•ì¶©, HBM ìŠ¤íƒì˜ ì—´Â·ì‹ ë¢°ì„± ì´ìŠˆ ëŒ€ì‘(ë²ˆì¸Â·í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ì»¤ë²„ë¦¬ì§€, ì—´ì„¤ê³„ ë§ˆì§„ ê²€ì¦)ì´ ì‹œê¸‰í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë™ì‹œì— ê³ ê°Â·ì œí’ˆ ì§‘ì¤‘ë„ë¥¼ KPIë¡œ ê´€ë¦¬í•˜ë©° ë“€ì–¼ì†Œì‹±Â·ë©€í‹°ë²¤ë” ë° ê°€ê²©ì§€ìˆ˜ ì—°ë™/í…Œì´í¬ì˜¤ì–´í˜ì´ ì¥ê¸°ê³„ì•½ì„ í™œìš©í•˜ê³ , HBM í¸ì¤‘ì„ DDR5Â·CXLÂ·ë°ì´í„°ì„¼í„° SSDì™€ íŒŒìš´ë“œë¦¬ì˜ AI ASIC/NPUÂ·FPGA ë“±ìœ¼ë¡œ ë¶„ì‚°í•´ ë³€ë™ì„±ì„ í¡ìˆ˜í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¯¸Â·ì¤‘ ê·œì œì™€ ì¤‘êµ­ ë°˜ë…ì  ë“± ì§€ì •í•™ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ì „ì œë¡œ ìˆ˜ìš” ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ë³„ CapExÂ·ì›¨ì´í¼ ìŠ¤íƒ€íŠ¸Â·ì¸ë ¥ ê°€ë³€ê³„íšì„ ë§ˆë ¨í•˜ê³ , NVIDIA ì™¸ AMD/IntelÂ·í•˜ì´í¼ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¼ëŸ¬Â·ì¤‘êµ­ ëŒ€ì²´ ê°€ì†ê¸°ì™€ì˜ í˜‘ì—…ìœ¼ë¡œ ìƒíƒœê³„ë¥¼ ë‹¤ë³€í™”í•˜ì‹­ì‹œì˜¤. Due to the booming AI server market, HBM, CoWoS/2.5D/3D packaging, and test processes are becoming bottlenecks, making it urgent to strengthen the yield management system, expand equipment lead time and capacity, and address thermal and reliability issues of HBM stacks (burn-in, test coverage, thermal design margin verification). Simultaneously, manage customer and product concentration as a KPI, leverage dual-sourcing, multi-vendor strategies, and long-term contracts linked to price indices and/or take-or-pay agreements, and diversify away from HBM concentration towards DDR5, CXL, data center SSDs, and foundry's AI ASIC/NPU/FPGA to absorb volatility. Premised on geopolitical risks such as US-China regulations and China's anti-monopoly measures, prepare variable plans for CapEx, wafer starts, and manpower for each demand scenario, and diversify the ecosystem through collaboration with AMD/Intel, hyperscalers, and alternative Chinese accelerators, beyond NVIDIA.

While the Korean semiconductor industry is enjoying a boom driven by NVIDIA-centric HBM demand, it is pointed out that single customer dependence, geopolitical factors, regulatory changes, and product roadmap fluctuations pose significant risks. From a manufacturing perspective, key action points include HBM/packaging capacity and yield management; risk hedging through top-tier customer proportion KPIs, long-term supply contracts, and dual sourcing; portfolio diversification (e.g., DDR5, CXL, data center SSDs); diversifying customers to include NVIDIA, AMD, Intel, and in-house chip customers; and scenario-based CapEx and wafer start adjustments in preparation for regulatory changes. Cycle volatility must also be absorbed by strengthening quality and reliability (thermal/test coverage) and implementing multi-layered inventory and contract structures.

The analysis that the core constraint on AI development is 'power' rather than 'capital' provides direct strategic implications for manufacturing AX. The US may be slow to respond to AI demand due to power infrastructure and permitting bottlenecks, while China's expansion of renewables, nuclear power, and gas could strengthen its AI power foundation. Manufacturers must optimize the deployment of AI workloads (edge/cloud), scheduling (off-peak/DR), on-site power sources (renewables + ESS, CHP), and the choice of PPA/tariff, considering power availability and carbon intensity. Furthermore, demanding energy and carbon transparency from AI vendors and establishing a system to simultaneously manage cost, ESG, and performance with KPIs like kWh/task and gCO2/task are practical action points.

í†µí•© ì¸ì‚¬ì´íŠ¸:Consolidated Insight:
AI ê¸°ë°˜ ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ë§ì€ ìƒì‚° ë³€ë™Â·ê²°ê·¼Â·ìì¬ ì§€ì—° ë“± ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì— ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ëŒ€ì‘í•´ ì¸ë ¥ì„ ì¬ë°°ì¹˜í•˜ê³ , ìŠ¤í‚¬ ë§¤íŠ¸ë¦­ìŠ¤Â·ë…¸ë¬´ ê·œì •Â·ê°€ìš©ì‹œê°„ê³¼ ERP/MES ë°ì´í„°ë¥¼ í†µí•©í•´ ì•ˆì „Â·í’ˆì§ˆ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ì™€ ì´ˆê³¼ê·¼ë¬´Â·ê³„ì•½ì§ ì˜ì¡´ì„ ì¤„ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤ì œë¡œ 166,000ê±´ì˜ êµëŒ€/íœ´ë¬´ ìš”ì²­ ìë™ ì²˜ë¦¬, ì»´í”Œë¼ì´ì–¸ìŠ¤ 70% ê°œì„ , ìƒì‚°ì„± 5~10% í–¥ìƒ, ê³„ì•½ì§ 50% ì¶•ì†Œ, ì´ì§ë¥  ìµœëŒ€ 5%p ê°œì„ , ì´ˆê³¼ê·¼ë¬´ë¹„ìš© ìµœëŒ€ 10% ì ˆê°ì´ ë³´ê³ ë˜ì—ˆìœ¼ë©°, ëª¨ë°”ì¼ ì…€í”„ì„œë¹„ìŠ¤ì™€ ê³µì •í•œ ì„ í˜¸ ë°˜ì˜ì´ ìœ ì§€ìœ¨ì„ ë†’ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë„ì…ì€ ë³€ë™ì„± ë†’ì€ ë¼ì¸ íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿ â†’ êµëŒ€ êµí™˜ ê°€ë“œë ˆì¼(ìê²©Â·ê·¼ë¬´ì‹œê°„Â·íœ´ì‹ ê·œì •) ì„¤ì • â†’ KPI(OTìœ¨Â·ê³¼ë°°ì¹˜ìœ¨Â·ê²°ê·¼ ì»¤ë²„ë¦¬ì§€Â·ìŠ¤ì™‘ ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„) ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§Â·íŠœë‹ ìˆœìœ¼ë¡œ ì§„í–‰í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ íš¨ê³¼ì ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. AI-based scheduling responds in real-time to events such as production fluctuations, absenteeism, and material delays to reallocate personnel, and by integrating skill matrices, labor regulations, available time, and ERP/MES data, it reduces safety and quality risks and reliance on overtime and contract workers. In practice, automatic processing of 166,000 shift/leave requests, a 70% improvement in compliance, a 5-10% improvement in productivity, a 50% reduction in contract workers, up to a 5 percentage point improvement in turnover rate, and up to a 10% reduction in overtime costs have been reported. Mobile self-service and fair consideration of preferences increase retention rates. Implementation is effective when proceeding in the following order: pilot on high-variability lines â†’ setting shift exchange guardrails (qualification, working hours, rest regulations) â†’ monitoring and tuning KPIs (overtime rate, over-allocation rate, absenteeism coverage, swap lead time).

In manufacturing sites, adopt an architecture that separates GPUs (for large-scale training, fine-tuning, domain adaptation, synthetic data) and NPUs (for on-site inference such as vision inspection, robots, predictive maintenance, and process control), and for each process, hybridly deploy on-premise NPUs, factory edge, and public and national GPUs based on latency, security, and cost. Manage TCO with model lightweighting (quantization, pruning, sparsity, KV caching) and manufacturing MLOps and governance, and proactively establish power and cooling (PUE improvement, liquid cooling/immersion cooling) and regulatory and security systems. Additionally, by utilizing the national 260,000 GPU infrastructure and academic and domestic semiconductor testbeds for PoC, adoption risks can be reduced and the speed of wider adoption can be accelerated.

A national-level strategy for large-scale GPU expansion and NPU integration can accelerate the AI transformation of manufacturing. Through pilot collaboration with domestic AI semiconductors and public resources, costs can be lowered and adoption speed can be increased.

The expansion of 300MW~1GW-class AI data centers by the domestic big three telcos and the introduction of liquid cooling and high-density GPUs provide manufacturers with a practical option to safely offload large-scale AI workloads such as vision inspection, predictive maintenance, and digital twins to off-site infrastructure. Reducing latency through dedicated lines, private 5G, and MEC connectivity built on a nationwide network supports real-time inference for robotics and autonomous mobile entities. A hybrid/multi-cloud design, capacity reservation (reserved instances, colocation), and SLAs including PUE and RE100 are all actionable strategies. Considering the competition for GPU supply and demand and changes in cost structure, determine the optimal combination of in-house construction and utilizing telco data centers early.

The three major domestic telecom companies are aggressively expanding their large-scale AI data centers (targeting up to 1GW, with an operational goal of 300MW, and securing over 500MW) and introducing high-density GPU infrastructure such as liquid cooling. This signifies a foundation for manufacturers to utilize large-scale AI training and inference domestically with low latency and high reliability. Manufacturers can adopt the following as implementation points: 1) Optimizing factory-DC connectivity with dedicated lines/Private 5G, 2) Securing GPU capacity through reserved instances, colocation, etc., 3) Hybrid design considering multi-cloud and data sovereignty, 4) ESG-friendly SLA linked with PUE and renewable energy, 5) Enabling real-time robotics and digital twins through MEC/edge DC selection.

Amidst the tension between the government's 61% reduction target and surging electricity demand for AI and semiconductors, manufacturers need realistic reduction and electricity strategies focused on 'minimizing emissions per unit' to reduce the risk of overseas relocation. An effective portfolio combines load shaping (switching AI training/deployment during nighttime/low-load periods), process heat recovery, high-efficiency motors/pumps, compressed air leak management, AI-based BEMS/FEMS optimization, DR participation, long-term PPA/REC, and onsite PV+ESS. For new construction and expansions, site and timing should be determined by indexing regional electricity connection capacity, unit costs, renewable energy availability, and outage risks; supply chains should be diversified based on TCO+Carbon criteria; and cost structures should be redesigned with carbon budgets per product.

The report quantitatively shows that due to tariffs, the average input costs for New York manufacturing rose by approximately 20%, and 75% experienced a decline in profitability despite passing on costs, with import-dependent electronics and computer sectors being particularly vulnerable. From a manufacturing AX perspective, it is key to agilely adjust procurement, production, and inventory decisions by evaluating BOM unit tariff sensitivity and 5/10/25% scenarios with digital twins to recalculate delivery times and margins, and by enabling ERP integration of raw material/tariff linkage in long-term contracts, multisourcing, cost-to-serve based dynamic pricing, and automatic re-evaluation of HS codes and country of origin. Under policy uncertainty, buffer cash flow risks through phased CAPEX execution and energy cost hedging and load schedule optimization.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì´ ë³´ê³ ì„œëŠ” ê´€ì„¸ë¡œ ì¸í•œ ì›ìì¬Â·ì—ë„ˆì§€Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜Â·ê±´ì„¤ ë¹„ìš© ê¸‰ë“±ê³¼ ìˆ˜ìš”ìœ„ì¶•ì´ ë‰´ìš• ì œì¡°ì—… ì „ë°˜ì— ë¯¸ì¹˜ëŠ” ì •ëŸ‰ì  ì¦ê±°ë¥¼ ì œì‹œí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡° AX ê´€ì ì—ì„œ ì´ëŠ” ê³µê¸‰ë§ ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆ, AI ìˆ˜ìš”Â·ê°€ê²©Â·ì¡°ë‹¬ ìµœì í™”, ì—ë„ˆì§€ ë¶€í•˜Â·í—¤ì§€ ì „ëµ, ë©€í‹°ì†Œì‹±Â·BOM ì¬ì„¤ê³„, ê³„ì•½ ì¸ë±ì‹± ë“± ì‹¤í–‰ ê³¼ì œë¥¼ ì¦‰ì‹œ ì¶”ì§„í•´ì•¼ í•¨ì„ ì˜ë¯¸í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. íŠ¹íˆ ê´€ì„¸ ë¯¼ê°ë„ ê¸°ë°˜ì˜ ë¶€í’ˆ ëŒ€ì²´, ë¹„ìš©-ê°€ê²© ì—°ê³„ ê°•í™”, í˜„ì¥ í’ˆì§ˆ/ìŠ¤í¬ë© ì €ê° ìë™í™”ë¡œ ë§ˆì§„ì„ ë°©ì–´í•˜ê³ , ì •ì±… ë³€ë™ì„ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ë°ì´í„°ë¡œ í¡ìˆ˜í•˜ëŠ” ìš´ì˜ì²´ê³„ë¥¼ êµ¬ì¶•í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ í•µì‹¬ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. This report provides quantitative evidence of the surge in raw material, energy, logistics, and construction costs and demand contraction caused by tariffs, affecting New York's manufacturing sector as a whole. From a manufacturing AX perspective, this implies the immediate need to pursue action items such as supply chain digital twin, AI-driven demand, pricing, and procurement optimization, energy load and hedging strategies, multi-sourcing and BOM redesign, and contract indexing. Specifically, the key is to defend margins through component substitution based on tariff sensitivity, strengthened cost-price linkage, and automation of on-site quality/scrap reduction, while also establishing an operating system that absorbs policy changes with real-time data.

Domestic manufacturing conglomerates are reorganizing their organizations around 'speed, practical skills, and generational change' in response to AI transformation and global uncertainties, placing young leaders with field/technical capabilities and joint leadership (e.g., co-CEOs) at the forefront. In terms of execution, the introduction of a BU/factory unit two-in-a-box system (operational responsibility + data and automation leader), the expansion of line leaders' digital budget authority and production engineers' P&L roles, AI PoC to mass production conversion rate and lead time KPIs, skill-based HR, and scenario-based CAPEX and supply chain diversification are effective. Through this, they can accelerate the alignment of strategy, field operations, and technology, and enhance manufacturing AX execution capabilities.

êµ­ë‚´ ëŒ€ê¸°ì—…ì˜ ì—°ë§ ì¸ì‚¬ëŠ” â€˜ì†ë„Â·ì‹¤ìš©Â·ì„¸ëŒ€êµì²´â€™ë¥¼ í•µì‹¬ìœ¼ë¡œ, ì˜¤ë„ˆê²½ì˜ ë³µê·€ì™€ íˆ¬í†±(ê³µë™CEO) í™•ëŒ€ë¡œ ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì •ê³¼ ì‹¤í–‰ë ¥ì„ ëŒì–´ì˜¬ë¦¬ë ¤ëŠ” íë¦„ì´ë‹¤. ì œì¡° ê´€ì ì—ì„œëŠ” í˜„ì¥Â·ê¸°ìˆ  ì—­ëŸ‰ ì¤‘ì‹¬ì˜ ì¸ì‚¬ì™€ ë‘ ì¶•(ì‚¬ì—…/ê¸°ìˆ ) ë¦¬ë”ì‹­ì´ AIÂ·ìë™í™” ê³¼ì œë¥¼ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ í˜„ì¥ì— ë‚´ë¦¬ëŠ” ë° ìœ íš¨í•˜ë‹¤. ê³µì¥/BU ë‹¨ìœ„ two-in-a-box ëª¨ë¸ ë„ì…, ì—”ì§€ë‹ˆì–´ì˜ P&L ì—­í•  í™•ëŒ€, AI PoCâ†’ì–‘ì‚° ì „í™˜ìœ¨Â·ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì • ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„ KPIí™”, ì§ë¬´ ìŠ¤í‚¬ ë§¤íŠ¸ë¦­ìŠ¤ ê¸°ë°˜ ì¸ì‚¬, ê³µê¸‰ë§ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ ëŒ€ì‘ì„ ìœ„í•œ ì„ ì œ ì¬í¸ ë“±ì´ ì‹¤ì²œ í¬ì¸íŠ¸ë‹¤. The year-end personnel reshuffles of domestic large corporations are centered on 'speed, practicality, and generational change,' reflecting a trend to boost decision-making and execution capabilities through the return to owner-management and the expansion of a two-top (co-CEO) system. From a manufacturing perspective, personnel management centered on on-site and technical capabilities, along with two-pillar (business/technology) leadership, is effective in rapidly deploying AI and automation initiatives to the field. Practical points include the introduction of a two-in-a-box model at the factory/BU level, expansion of engineers' P&L roles, KPI-setting for AI PoC to mass production conversion rate and decision-making lead time, personnel management based on job skill matrices, and proactive reorganization to respond to supply chain risks.
